< review>
This place is located in PS business park (Commerce Park) cross street from NVIDIA new building in walsh ave.
I ordered from them sometimes the grilled chicken sandwich and Caesar salad in lunch time.
The place is packed and hard to find a place to seat from noon to 1pm, because simply it is the only place avaiable in that area to have lunch. The owner is very friendly and nice guy.
the waiting time is not bad during busy time around 10 minutes.
they close after 2:30pm , I went there for a late lunch but I've told they close early, if you want to get your lunch peacefully you have to go around 11:30am.
in general this place is clean and the food is delicious.< /review>

< Review>
We hired Sullivan to do our solar after receiving quotes from 5 other companies.  We ultimately chose Sullivan for numerous reasons and it wasn't because they were the cheapest.

<Rating>4</Rating>< Text>
Very clean, efficient, newer, attractive. Trying to figure out destinations for Metrolink is extremely confusing. There's very little information and there's no wall maps like you see in BART or other major cities. I'm not sure how to buy tickets either. I find the biggest concern with people who haven't tried Metrolink yet is the concern they will be dropped off at a station in the middle of nowhere, stranded without having a clue when the next train is going to come. The Artic station could do 10 times as much business with Metrolink if they stopped trying to run it like Amtrak. Congratulations you've found Los Angeles!< /Text>

<review>So i dont know are people asking if they ought to take greyhound to Los Angeles or are they asking if the Anaheim station is clean or what do people want to know? Well i been taking greyhound for  a long time and  each driver is different. but when you dont have a lot of money and are trying to travel this is usually the way to go unless you can go on Megabus which sometimes has some amazing deals but you have to have a phone to purchase tix with Mega bus. IT does take a longer time to travel by bus but as far as i am concerned its the cheapest way to travel . Sometimes you get a nice group with you on the bus and other times  it can be a little shady. But if you plan ahead either way you get good deals.The Anaheim Arctic station is a nice clean station to my knowledge. However just so you know if you are ever stranded in the Anaheim station they do close at 2am and to my knowledge no one is allowed in the station after 2am even if you have a ticket so plan ahead. Now in DTLA Union station if you have an Amtrak ticket i know you are allowed to stay in the station overnight and or until your Amtrak train -bus arrives. Or if you are metro link  monthly passholder. If you are traveling any other way they wont let you stay in the station until 4am so your stuck outside if you are a metro pass holder which sucks if you dont have a lot of money . Union station has Starbucks subway and a little mini mart and so does the Anaheim Arctic( mini mart)  but no Starbucks in Anaheim station and no subway either. Very pricey i think in Anaheim actually if you want to go to the restaurant upstairs or  the pink berry or mini mart. Greyhound now has outlets to charge phone. if you travel greyhound you should carry snacks as they do not carry. Amtrak has a cafe car unless there is a woops then they close. If you are trying to get into Los Angeles from Anaheim or Orange there are even cheaper ways to get there but it will take you double the time.  OCTA bus 50 to LBT 90's ( ask 4 transfer) to Blue line Metro. or Octa bus 50 or Octa 46 and walk a block north or south depending which line and take METRO 460 to DTLA. OCTA bus 42 to LBT 173 trnsfr MetroGreenLine/Blue line. ALL the best!< /review>< Pictures>

I spent quite a while driving around getting the quotes (each buyer needed to see and test what they would be buying), but when I had all the information, I ended up back at Wilshire Coin Exchange.  Their estimate beat the other two businesses by $45 dollars or more and the staff couldn't have been nicer.  If I ever have need of similar services again, I now know where to go.< /Text>

<gmapID>0x80c3533cf4962aaf:0x2d16d702949eb0d2< /gmapID><text>As of July 2017, this is a pretty new Motel 6; at least, the interior is new.

It was nice not to have ash trays in the room, finally! There was a very slight tobacco odor, though. It was not bad, but there were two cigarette burns on the tub. Some people just don't obey the rules!

Many of the bright-white towels had some type of mark on them. I suppose it is really hard to get stains out of white towels. They were grey and another had bright red fingernail polish on it.

There is a security guard during the day; but, they really need one at night to keep the locals from roaming through the parking lot. One guy was collecting cans at 4:30 in the morning. <user_name>Lance Hotz</user_name><user_id>103631969221744636883<//user_id>< Text>
This is going to be long and I apologize. If you only plan to spend two or three nights then this is a good place for you. If you are looking for a homey kind of room and planning for a longer stay you might need to look elsewhere. But please keep in mind this is a budget motel. Even with the negatives I would give this location three and a half stars.

My wife and I had to rent a motel room for several days while waiting for our new residence to be ready.
We chose Motel Six because it was pet friendly for our little dog. This Motel Six is not in the best area, with working girls around and doing what working girls do. However within the motel area we did feel secure. The room we stayed in was a very large corner room, over 200 square feet. The rooms have been recently remodeled and now they don't exactly shout "Welcome." Hospital sterile is not a good look, seriously.

The only things that break up the monotonous  walls are the window, an air conditioner, and a nice sized flat screen TV. There were no wall mounted lamps next to the large king size bed, not even the mandatory tacky artwork on the walls. The ceiling lighting is in keeping with the room design, recessed, white, and sterile, as if the designers didn't know they make flourescent light bulbs that duplicate the warm welcome feeling of the incandescent ones. In fact I even brought one of my own lamps from home.

The clothes hanging rack is miniscule, just two small posts protruding from the wall with not enough room between them to allow the hangers not to overlap each other. If you have more than eight items of clothing to hang I am afraid you are out of luck. Below that are three small shelves, the only places in this very large room to put folding clothes. Both of these will be an issue for any guy who has a wife or a girlfriend.

This leads to the lack of surfaces. There is a half table mounted to the wall along with two Spartan Ikea type chairs. The bathroom sink area didn't need to have such a small surface area, as to one side there was a fifteen inch empty space between it and the adjacent wall. Again remember the wives and girlfriends. There is no dresser or chest of drawers as is found in most motel rooms to store your clothes, thus there is no top surface on which to set anything either. In summary it is as if Motel 6 did the remodel on the cheap with no thought toward the convenience and comfort of its customers, especially leaving out wives and girlfriends.

That is too bad, since the staff there is great. I had no problems with the rudeness of the housekeeping staff of which other reviewers have mentioned. And if I did I wouldn't hold it against them. They are working at a hard minimum wage job, often with no tips for their good service. And the office staff are all very nice people, always willing to help with a friendly smile and that is a huge plus for travelers. I just wish that in this case at least Motel Six was on par with its employees.
PS: On the plus side Motel Six provides in room mini refrigerators. üòÅüòÅüòÅ<//Text>
